Witnesses there claimed that the MVD used excessive force and that they had instigated the fighting.\n</p><p>Further firefights between Armenian militiamen and Soviet troops occurred in <a href="/wiki/Nubarashen" class="mw-redirect" title="Nubarashen">Sovetashen</a>, near the capital and resulted in the deaths of over 26 people, mostly Armenians. The <a href="/wiki/Pogrom_of_Armenians_in_Baku" class="mw-redirect" title="Pogrom of Armenians in Baku">pogrom of Armenians in Baku</a> in January 1990 forced almost all of the 200,000 Armenians in the Azerbaijani capital <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> to flee to Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On 23 August 1990, Armenia declared its sovereignty on its territory. On 17 March 1991, Armenia, along with the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>, Georgia and <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldova</a>, boycotted a nationwide <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_referendum,_1991" title="Soviet Union referendum, 1991">referendum</a> in which 78% of all voters voted for the retention of the Soviet Union in a reformed form.<sup id="cite_ref-NewsBrief_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewsBrief-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_independence">Restoration of independence</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Armenia#Independent_Armenia_(1991-today)" title="History of Armenia">History of Armenia \xc2\xa7&#160;Independent Armenia (1991-today)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NKR_war.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NKR_war.JPG/220px-NKR_war.JPG" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NKR_war.JPG/330px-NKR_war.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NKR_war.JPG/440px-NKR_war.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1818" data-file-height="1228" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NKR_war.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Armenian soldiers during the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a></div></div></div>\n<p>On 21 September 1991, Armenia officially declared its independence after the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat attempt">failed August coup</a> in Moscow. <a href="/wiki/Levon_Ter-Petrosyan" title="Levon Ter-Petrosyan">Levon Ter-Petrosyan</a> was popularly elected the first President of the newly independent Republic of Armenia on 16 October 1991. He had risen to prominence by leading the <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_movement" title="Karabakh movement">Karabakh movement</a> for the unification of the Armenian-populated <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Croissant_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croissant-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On 26 December 1991, the Soviet Union ceased to exist and Armenia\'s independence was recognised.\n</p><p>Ter-Petrosyan led Armenia alongside Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Vazgen_Sargsyan" title="Vazgen Sargsyan">Vazgen Sargsyan</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> with neighbouring Azerbaijan. The initial post-Soviet years were marred by economic difficulties, which had their roots early in the Karabakh conflict when the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Popular_Front_Party" title="Azerbaijani Popular Front Party">Azerbaijani Popular Front</a> managed to pressure the Azerbaijan SSR to instigate a railway and air <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a> against Armenia. This move effectively crippled Armenia\'s economy as 85% of its cargo and goods arrived through rail traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-Croissant_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croissant-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, Turkey joined the blockade against Armenia in support of Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-GHF_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHF-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:September_21,_2011_parade,_Yerevan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg/170px-September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg/255px-September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg/340px-September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:September_21,_2011_parade,_Yerevan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 21 September 2011 parade in Yerevan, marking the 20th anniversary of Armenia\'s re-independence</div></div></div>\n<p>The Karabakh war ended after a Russian-brokered <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">cease-fire</a> was put in place in 1994. The war was a success for the Karabakh Armenian forces who managed to capture 16% of Azerbaijan\'s internationally recognised territory including Nagorno-Karabakh itself.<sup id="cite_ref-DeWaal_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeWaal-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Armenia and Azerbaijan have held peace talks, mediated by the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organisation for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE). The status of Karabakh has yet to be determined. The economies of both countries have been hurt in the absence of a complete resolution and Armenia\'s borders with Turkey and Azerbaijan remain closed. By the time both Azerbaijan and Armenia had finally agreed to a ceasefire in 1994, an estimated 30,000 people had been killed and over a million had been displaced.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As it enters the 21st century, Armenia faces many hardships. It has made a full switch to a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. One study ranks it the 41st most "economically free" nation in the world, as of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-economic-index_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economic-index-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Its relations with Europe, the Middle East, and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> have allowed Armenia to increase trade.<sup id="cite_ref-EPP_Group_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPP_Group-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Arka_news_agency_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arka_news_agency-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Gas, oil, and other supplies come through two vital routes: Iran and Georgia. Armenia maintains cordial relations with both countries.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Dialogue_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Dialogue-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenia_locator_map_ITA.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Armenia_locator_map_ITA.png/220px-Armenia_locator_map_ITA.png" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Armenia_locator_map_ITA.png 1.5x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="354" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenia_locator_map_ITA.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Armenia and neighbouring countries</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Armenia" title="Geography of Armenia">Geography of Armenia</a></div>\n<p>Armenia is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Geopolitical" class="mw-redirect" title="Geopolitical">geopolitical</a> <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcaucasus">Transcaucasus</a> (South Caucasus) region, that is located in the Southern <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> and their lowlands between the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>, and northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Highland" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Highland">Armenian Highlands</a>. Armenia is bordered on the north by <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, the east by <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>; the south by <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>; and the southwest and west by <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. Armenia lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/38th_parallel_north" title="38th parallel north">38\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42\xc2\xb0 N</a>, and meridians <a href="/wiki/43rd_meridian_east" title="43rd meridian east">43\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/47th_meridian_east" title="47th meridian east">47\xc2\xb0 E</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenien_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Armenien_topo.jpg/220px-Armenien_topo.jpg" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Armenien_topo.jpg/330px-Armenien_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Armenien_topo.jpg/440px-Armenien_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1314" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenien_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Armenia\'s mountainous and volcanic <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Republic of Armenia has a territorial area of 29,743 square kilometres (11,484&#160;sq&#160;mi). The terrain is mostly mountainous, with fast flowing rivers, and few forests. The land rises to 4,090 metres (13,419 feet) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Aragats" title="Mount Aragats">Mount Aragats</a>, and no point is below 390 metres (1,280&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_average_elevation" title="List of countries by average elevation">Average elevation of the country</a> area is 10th highest in the world.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Mount Ararat</dt></dl>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a>, which was historically part of Armenia, is the highest mountain in the region. Now located in Turkey, but clearly visible from Armenia, it is regarded by the Armenians as a symbol of their land. Because of this, the mountain is present on the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Armenia" title="Coat of arms of Armenia">Armenian national emblem</a> today.<sup id="cite_ref-Azarian2007_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Azarian2007-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Adalian2010_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adalian2010-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Minahan1998_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan1998-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Armenia" title="Climate of Armenia">Climate of Armenia</a></div>\n<p>The climate in Armenia is markedly highland <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a>. Summers are dry and sunny, lasting from June to mid-September. The temperature fluctuates between 22 and 36&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72 and 97&#160;\xc2\xb0F). However, the low humidity level mitigates the effect of high temperatures. Evening breezes blowing down the mountains provide a welcome refreshing and cooling effect. Springs are short, while autumns are long. Autumns are known for their vibrant and colourful foliage.\n</p><p>Winters are quite cold with plenty of snow, with temperatures ranging between \xe2\x88\x9210 and \xe2\x88\x925&#160;\xc2\xb0C (14 and 23&#160;\xc2\xb0F). <a href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">Winter sports</a> enthusiasts enjoy skiing down the hills of <a href="/wiki/Tsakhkadzor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsakhkadzor">Tsakhkadzor</a>, located thirty minutes outside Yerevan. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Sevan" title="Lake Sevan">Lake Sevan</a>, nestled up in the Armenian highlands, is the second largest lake in the world relative to its altitude, at 1,900 metres (6,234&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_protection">Environment protection</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia,_Azerbaijan,_Georgia,_Russia,_Germany,_Italy,_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg/220px-CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg/330px-CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg/440px-CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="658" data-file-height="362" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia,_Azerbaijan,_Georgia,_Russia,_Germany,_Italy,_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Carbon dioxide emissions in metric tons per capita in Armenia, Azerbaijan, Georgia, Russia, Germany, Italy, USA in 2000\xe2\x80\x932012. World Bank data.</div></div></div>\n<p>Armenia ranked 63rd out of 180 countries on <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a> (EPI) in 2018. Its rank on subindex Environmental Health (which is weighted at 40% in EPI) is 109, while Armenia\'s rank on subindex of Ecosystem Vitality (weighted at 60% in EPI) is 27th best in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> This suggests that main environmental issues in Armenia are with <a href="/wiki/Armenia#Health" title="Armenia">population health</a>, while environment vitality is of lesser concern. Out of sub-subindices contributing to Environmental Health subindex ranking on Air Quality to which population is exposed is particularly unsatisfying.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Waste_management_in_Armenia" title="Waste management in Armenia">Waste management in Armenia</a> is underdeveloped, as no waste sorting or recycling takes place at Armenia\'s 60 landfills. A waste processing plant is scheduled for construction near <a href="/wiki/Hrazdan" title="Hrazdan">Hrazdan</a> city, which will allow for closure of 10 waste dumps.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite the availability of abundant renewable energy sources in Armenia (especially <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>) and calls from EU officials to shut down the <a href="/wiki/Metsamor_Nuclear_Power_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Metsamor Nuclear Power Plant">nuclear power plant at Metsamor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> the Armenian Government is exploring the possibilities of installing new small modular nuclear reactors. In 2018 existing nuclear plant is scheduled for modernization to enhance its safety and increase power production by about 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Armenian Ministry of Nature Protection introduced taxes for air and water pollution and solid-waste disposal, whose revenues are used for environmental protection activities.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Armenia" title="Government of Armenia">Government of Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Armenia" title="Politics of Armenia">Politics of Armenia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg/220px-Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg/330px-Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg/440px-Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_Yerevan_building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Armenia)" title="National Assembly (Armenia)">National Assembly</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Armenia" title="Politics of Armenia">Politics of Armenia</a> takes place in a framework of  <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative</a>  <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democratic</a> republic. Until transition in April 2018 Armenian constitution adhered to the model of <a href="/wiki/Semi-Presidential_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-Presidential Republic">semi-presidential republic</a>. \n</p><p>According to the current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Armenia" title="Constitution of Armenia">Constitution of Armenia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Armenia" title="President of Armenia">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> holding largely representational functions, while the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Armenia" title="Prime Minister of Armenia">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and exercises <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a>. \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative power</a> is vested in the <a href="/wiki/Unicameral_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral parliament">unicameral parliament</a> is also called the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Armenia">Azgayin Zhoghov</a> or <i><a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Armenia">National Assembly</a>.</i>\n</p><p>Armenia has universal suffrage above the age of eighteen.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Armenia" title="Foreign relations of Armenia">Foreign relations of Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenia and the European Union">Armenia and the European Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenia%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="Armenia\xe2\x80\x93Turkey relations">Armenia\xe2\x80\x93Turkey relations</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moscow,_embassy_of_Armenia_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Moscow%2C_embassy_of_Armenia_%282%29.jpg/170px-Moscow%2C_embassy_of_Armenia_%282%29.jpg" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Moscow%2C_embassy_of_Armenia_%282%29.jpg/255px-Moscow%2C_embassy_of_Armenia_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Moscow%2C_embassy_of_Armenia_%282%29.jpg/340px-Moscow%2C_embassy_of_Armenia_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1352" data-file-height="1774" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moscow,_embassy_of_Armenia_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Armenia_in_Moscow" class="mw-redirect" title="Embassy of Armenia in Moscow">Embassy of Armenia in Moscow</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Armenia presently maintains positive relations with almost every country in the world, with two major exceptions being its immediate neighbours, Turkey and Azerbaijan. Tensions were running high between Armenians and Azerbaijanis during the final years of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> dominated the region\'s politics throughout the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-CFR-9148_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFR-9148-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> To this day, Armenia\'s borders with Turkey and Azerbaijan are under severe blockade. In addition, a permanent solution for the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict has not been reached despite the mediation provided by organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>.\n</p><p>Armenia is a member of more than 40 international organisations, including the United Nations; the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>; the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>; <a href="/wiki/World_Customs_Organization" title="World Customs Organization">World Customs Organization</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Black_Sea_Economic_Cooperation" title="Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation">Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">CSTO</a> military alliance, and also participates in NATO\'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> program.\n</p><p>Turkey also has a long history of poor relations with Armenia over its refusal to acknowledge the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a>, even though it was one of the first countries to recognize the Republic of Armenia (the 3rd republic) after its independence from the USSR in 1991. Despite this, for most of the 20th century and early 21st century, relations remain tense and there are no formal diplomatic relations between the two countries due to Turkey\'s refusal to establish them for numerous reasons. During the Nagorno-Karabakh War, and citing it as the reason, Turkey illegally closed its border with Armenia in 1993. It has not lifted its blockade despite pressure from the powerful Turkish business lobby interested in Armenian markets.<sup id="cite_ref-CFR-9148_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFR-9148-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 October 2009, Armenia and Turkey signed protocols on the normalisation of relations, which set a timetable for restoring diplomatic ties and reopening their joint border.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The ratification of those had to be made in the national parliaments. In Armenia, it passed through the legislatively required approval of the Constitutional Court and was sent to parliament for final ratification. The President had made multiple public announcements, both in Armenia and abroad, that, as the leader of the political majority of Armenia, he assured the ratification of the protocols if Turkey also ratified them. Despite this, the process stopped, as Turkey continuously added more preconditions to its ratification and also "delayed it beyond any reasonable time-period".\n</p><p>Due to its position between two unfriendly neighbours, Armenia has close security ties with Russia. At the request of the Armenian government, Russia maintains a <a href="/wiki/Russian_102nd_Military_Base" title="Russian 102nd Military Base">military base</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Gyumri" title="Gyumri">Gyumri</a> located in Northwestern Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-Armenia-base_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armenia-base-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> as a deterrent against Turkey.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Despite this, Armenia has also been looking toward Euro-Atlantic structures in recent years. It maintains good relations with the United States especially through its <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian diaspora</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census" title="United States Census">US Census Bureau</a>, there are 427,822 Armenians living in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because of the illicit border blockades by Azerbaijan and Turkey, Armenia continues to maintain solid relations with its southern neighbour Iran especially in the economic sector. Economic projects such a gas pipeline going from Iran to Armenia are being developed.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian President <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd" title="Tsitsernakaberd">Armenian Genocide memorial</a> in Yerevan</div></div></div>\n<p>Armenia is also a member of the Council of Europe, maintaining friendly relations with the European Union, especially with its member states such as France and Greece. A 2005 survey reported that 64% of Armenia\'s population would be in favour of joining the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Several Armenian officials have also expressed the desire for their country to eventually become an EU member state,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (January 2016)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> predicting that it will make an official bid for membership in a few years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 2004 its forces joined <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a>, a NATO-led international force in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>. It is also an observer member of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Community" title="Eurasian Economic Community">Eurasian Economic Community</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Armenian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian SSR">A former republic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, Armenia is an <a href="/wiki/Emergent_democracy" title="Emergent democracy">emerging democracy</a> and as of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> was negotiating with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> to become an associate partner. Legally speaking, it has the right to be considered as a prospective EU member provided it meets necessary standards and criteria, although officially such a plan does not exist in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The Government of Armenia, however, has joined the <a href="/wiki/Customs_Union_of_Belarus,_Kazakhstan_and_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan and Russia">Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan and Russia</a><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurasian Union">Eurasian Economic Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Armenia is included in the European Union\'s <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> (ENP) which aims at bringing the EU and its neighbours closer. The EU-Armenia Comprehensive and Enhanced Partnership Agreement (CEPA) was signed on 24 November 2017. Among other goals, it aims at improving investment climate.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Armenia" title="Human rights in Armenia">Human rights in Armenia</a></div>\n<p>Human rights in Armenia tend to be better than those in most <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">former Soviet republics</a> and have drawn closer to acceptable standards, especially economically.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Still, there are several considerable problems. Overall, the country is classified "partly free" by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>, which gives it a score of 45 in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Armenia" title="Armed Forces of Armenia">Armed Forces of Armenia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenianarmya.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Armenianarmya.jpg/220px-Armenianarmya.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Armenianarmya.jpg/330px-Armenianarmya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Armenianarmya.jpg/440px-Armenianarmya.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="259" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenianarmya.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Armenian_Army" title="Armenian Army">Armenian Army</a> <a href="/wiki/BTR-80" title="BTR-80">BTR-80s</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg/220px-2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg/330px-2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg/440px-2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade-8.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Armenian soldiers at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade" title="2010 Moscow Victory Day Parade">2010 Moscow Victory Day Parade</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Army" title="Armenian Army">Armenian Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Air_Force" title="Armenian Air Force">Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Air_Force" title="Armenian Air Force">Air Defence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Border_Guard" title="Armenian Border Guard">Border Guard</a> comprise the four branches of the Armed Forces of the Republic of Armenia. The Armenian military was formed after the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1985%E2%80%9391)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Soviet Union (1985\xe2\x80\x9391)">collapse of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991 and with the establishment of the Ministry of Defence in 1992. The <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> of the military is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Armenia" title="President of Armenia">President of Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serzh_Sargsyan" title="Serzh Sargsyan">Serzh Sargsyan</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ministry_(collective_executive)" title="Ministry (collective executive)">The Ministry</a> of Defence is in charge of political leadership, currently headed by <a href="/wiki/Colonel_general" title="Colonel general">Colonel General</a> <a href="/wiki/Seyran_Ohanyan" title="Seyran Ohanyan">Seyran Ohanyan</a>, while military command remains in the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Staff_(military)" title="Staff (military)">General Staff</a>, headed by the Chief of Staff, who is currently Colonel General <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Khatchaturov" title="Yuri Khatchaturov">Yuri Khatchaturov</a>.\n</p><p>Active forces now number about 81,000 soldiers, with an additional <a href="/wiki/Military_reserve_force" title="Military reserve force">reserve</a> of 32,000 troops. Armenian border guards are in charge of patrolling the country\'s borders with <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, while Russian troops continue to monitor its borders with <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. In the case of an attack, Armenia is able to mobilise every able-bodied man between the age of 15 and 59, with military preparedness.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a>, which establishes comprehensive limits on key categories of military equipment, was ratified by the Armenian parliament in July 1992. In March 1993, Armenia signed the multilateral <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Weapons_Convention" title="Chemical Weapons Convention">Chemical Weapons Convention</a>, which calls for the eventual elimination of chemical weapons. Armenia acceded to the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> (NPT) as a non-nuclear weapons state in July 1993.\n</p><p>Armenia is member of <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">Collective Security Treaty Organisation</a> (CSTO) along with <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>. It participates in NATO\'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> (PiP) program and is in a NATO organisation called <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a> (EAPC). Armenia has engaged in a peacekeeping mission in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> as part of non-NATO <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a> troops under Greek command.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Armenia also had 46 members of its military <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> forces as a part of the <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">Coalition Forces</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> until October 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Armenia" title="Administrative divisions of Armenia">Administrative divisions of Armenia</a></div>\n<div role="img" class="noresize" style="width: 386px; float: right; clear: right; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative; max-width: 100%; overflow-x: auto;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Armenia_template.svg/386px-Armenia_template.svg.png" width="386" height="394" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Armenia_template.svg/579px-Armenia_template.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Armenia_template.svg/772px-Armenia_template.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="725" data-file-height="740" />\n<div style="position:absolute; left:35px; top:60px"><a href="/wiki/Shirak_Province" title="Shirak Province">Shirak</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:114px; top:49px"><a href="/wiki/Lori_Province" title="Lori Province">Lori</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:183px; top:62px"><a href="/wiki/Tavush" class="mw-redirect" title="Tavush">Tavush</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:47px; top:139px"><a href="/wiki/Aragatsotn" class="mw-redirect" title="Aragatsotn">Aragatsotn</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:52px; top:177px"><a href="/wiki/Armavir_Province" title="Armavir Province">Armavir</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:104px; top:172px"><b><a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:146px; top:206px"><a href="/wiki/Ararat_Province" title="Ararat Province">Ararat</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:132px; top:142px"><a href="/wiki/Kotayk_Province" title="Kotayk Province">Kotayk</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:189px; top:149px"><a href="/wiki/Gegharkunik_Province" title="Gegharkunik Province">Gegharkunik</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:219px; top:225px"><a href="/wiki/Vayots_Dzor" class="mw-redirect" title="Vayots Dzor">Vayots<br />Dzor</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:302px; top:290px"><a href="/wiki/Syunik_Province" title="Syunik Province">Syunik</a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg/220px-%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg/330px-%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg/440px-%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4161" data-file-height="2747" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Geghard" title="Geghard">Geghard</a> monastery, <a href="/wiki/Kotayk_Province" title="Kotayk Province">Kotayk Province</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Armenia is divided into ten <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Armenia" title="Administrative divisions of Armenia">provinces</a> (<i>marzer</i>, singular <i>marz</i>), with the city (<i>kaghak</i>) of <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> (<span lang="hy" title="Armenian language text">\xd4\xb5\xd6\x80\xd6\x87\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb6</span>) having special administrative status as the country\'s capital. The chief executive in each of the ten provinces is the <i>marzpet</i> (<i>marz</i> governor), appointed by the government of Armenia. In Yerevan, the chief executive is the mayor, appointed by the president.\n</p><p>Within each province are <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of municipalities of Armenia">communities</a> (<i>hamaynkner</i>, singular <i>hamaynk</i>). Each community is self-governing and consists of one or more settlements (<i>bnakavayrer</i>, singular <i>bnakavayr</i>). Settlements are classified as either towns (<i>kaghakner</i>, singular <i>kaghak</i>) or villages (<i>gyugher</i>, singular <i>gyugh</i>). As of  2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Armenia includes 915 communities, of which 49 are considered urban and 866 are considered rural. The capital, Yerevan, also has the status of a community.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, Yerevan is divided into twelve semi-autonomous districts.\n</p>\n<table class="sortable wikitable" style="text-align:left; font-size:90%;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="font-size:100%; text-align:left;">\n<th colspan="2">Province\n</th>\n<th colspan="2">Capital\n</th>\n<th>Area (km\xc2\xb2)\n</th>\n<th>Population \xe2\x80\xa0\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Aragatsotn_Province" title="Aragatsotn Province">Aragatsotn</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" title="Armenian language text">\xd4\xb1\xd6\x80\xd5\xa1\xd5\xa3\xd5\xa1\xd5\xae\xd5\xb8\xd5\xbf\xd5\xb6</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ashtarak" style="text-align:right">2,086\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">254,397\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Lori_Province" title="Lori Province">Lori</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" text">\xd5\x8e\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb6\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb1\xd5\xb8\xd6\x80</span>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">3,799\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">235,537\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gyumri" title="Gyumri">Gyumri</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" title="Armenian language text">\xd4\xb3\xd5\xb5\xd5\xb8\xd6\x82\xd5\xb4\xd6\x80\xd5\xab</span>\n</td>\n<td title="Armenian language text">\xd5\x8d\xd5\xb5\xd5\xb8\xd6\x82\xd5\xb6\xd5\xab\xd6\x84</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Kapan" title="Kapan">Kapan</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" title="Armenian class="mw-redirect" title="Tavush">Tavush</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" title="Armenian language text">\xd5\x8f\xd5\xa1\xd5\xbe\xd5\xb8\xd6\x82\xd5\xb7</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ijevan" title="Ijevan">Ijevan</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" title="Armenian language text">\xd4\xbb\xd5\xbb\xd6\x87\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb6</span>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">2,704\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">128,609\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vayots_Dzor" class="mw-redirect" title="Vayots Dzor">Vayots Dzor</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" title="Armenian language text">\xd5\x8e\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb5\xd5\xb8\xd6\x81 \xd5\x81\xd5\xb8\xd6\x80</span>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Yeghegnadzor" title="Yeghegnadzor">Yeghegnadzor</a>&#160;&#160;</td>\n<td><span lang="hy" style="text-align:right">52,324\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a></td>\n<td><span lang="hy" title="Armenian language text">\xd4\xb5\xd6\x80\xd6\x87\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb6</span>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center">\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td style="text-align:center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">223\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">1,060,138\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>\xe2\x80\xa0 2011 census<br />Sources: Area and population of provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Armenia" title="Economy of Armenia">Economy of Armenia</a></div>\n<p>The economy relies heavily on investment and support from Armenians abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Before independence, Armenia\'s economy was largely industry-based \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>, machinery, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processed food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_rubber" title="Synthetic rubber">synthetic rubber</a>, and textile \xe2\x80\x93 and highly dependent on outside resources. The republic had developed a modern <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">industrial sector</a>, supplying <a href="/wiki/Machine_tool" title="Machine tool">machine tools</a>, textiles, and other <a href="/wiki/Final_goods" class="mw-redirect" title="Final goods">manufactured goods</a> to sister republics in exchange for raw materials and energy.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Recently, the <a href="/wiki/Intel_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel Corporation">Intel Corporation</a> agreed to open a research centre in Armenia, in addition to other technology companies, signalling the growth of the technology industry in Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Agriculture accounted for less than 20% of both <a href="/wiki/Net_material_product" title="Net material product">net material product</a> and <a href="/wiki/Full_employment" title="Full employment">total employment</a> before the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1985%E2%80%931991)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Soviet Union (1985\xe2\x80\x931991)">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991. After independence, the importance of agriculture in the economy increased markedly, its share at the end of the 1990s rising to more than 30% of GDP and more than 40% of total employment.<sup id="cite_ref-agri_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agri-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> This increase in the importance of agriculture was attributable to food security needs of the population in the face of uncertainty during the first phases of <a href="/wiki/Transition_economy" title="Transition economy">transition</a> and the collapse of the non-agricultural sectors of the economy in the early 1990s. As the economic situation stabilised and growth resumed, the share of agriculture in GDP dropped to slightly over 20% (2006 data), although the share of agriculture in employment remained more than 40%.<sup id="cite_ref-yb2007_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yb2007-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg/220px-Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg/330px-Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg/440px-Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> is the economic and cultural centre of Armenia.</div></div></div>\n<p>Armenian mines produce copper, zinc, gold, and lead. The vast majority of energy is produced with fuel imported from Russia, including gas and nuclear fuel (for its one nuclear power plant); the main domestic energy source is hydroelectric. Small deposits of coal, gas, and petroleum exist but have not yet been developed.\n</p><p>Like other <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">newly independent states</a> of the former Soviet Union, Armenia\'s economy suffers from the breakdown of former Soviet trading patterns. Soviet investment in and support of Armenian industry has virtually disappeared, so that few major enterprises are still able to function. In addition, the effects of the <a href="/wiki/1988_Armenian_earthquake" title="1988 Armenian earthquake">1988 Spitak earthquake</a>, which killed more than 25,000 people and made 500,000 homeless, are still being felt. The conflict with Azerbaijan over Nagorno-Karabakh has not been resolved. The closure of Azerbaijani and Turkish borders has devastated the economy, because Armenia depends on outside supplies of energy and most raw materials. Land routes through Georgia and Iran are inadequate or unreliable. The GDP fell nearly 60% between 1989 and 1993, but then resumed robust growth.<sup id="cite_ref-agri_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agri-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The national currency, the dram, suffered hyperinflation for the first years after its introduction in 1993.\n</p><p>Nevertheless, the government was able to make wide-ranging economic reforms that paid off in dramatically lower inflation and steady growth. The 1994 cease-fire in the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict has also helped the economy. Armenia has had strong economic growth since 1995, building on the turnaround that began the previous year, and inflation has been negligible for the past several years. New sectors, such as precious-stone processing and jewelry making, information and communication technology, and even tourism are beginning to supplement more traditional sectors of the economy, such as agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg/220px-Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg/330px-Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg/440px-Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Overdone_house_in_Yerevan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>New buildings in the <a href="/wiki/Ajapnyak_District" title="Ajapnyak District">Ajapnyak District</a> of Yerevan</div></div></div>\n<p>This steady economic progress has earned Armenia increasing support from international institutions. The <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a> (EBRD), and other <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_system" title="Global financial system">international financial institutions</a> (IFIs) and foreign countries are extending considerable grants and loans. Loans to Armenia since 1993 exceed $1.1&#160;billion. These loans are targeted at reducing the budget deficit and stabilising the currency; developing private businesses; energy; agriculture; food processing; transportation; the health and education sectors; and ongoing rehabilitation in the earthquake zone. The government joined the World Trade Organization on 5 February 2003. But one of the main sources of foreign direct investments remains the Armenian diaspora, which finances major parts of the reconstruction of infrastructure and other public projects. Being a growing democratic state, Armenia also hopes to get more financial aid from the Western World.\n</p><p>A liberal foreign investment law was approved in June 1994, and a law on privatization was adopted in 1997, as well as a program of state property privatization. Continued progress will depend on the ability of the government to strengthen its macroeconomic management, including increasing revenue collection, improving the investment climate, and making strides against corruption. However, unemployment, which was 18.5% in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> still remains a major problem due to the influx of thousands of refugees from the Karabakh conflict.\n</p><p>Armenia ranked 85th on the 2015 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UNDP</a> <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, the lowest among the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="South Caucasus">Transcaucasian</a> republics.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP2015_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP2015-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In 2016 estimates it climbed up to 84th position surpassing <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Armenia <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">ranks 47th</a> on inequality-adjusted human development index (IHDI) in 2016 report, ahead of all its neighboring countries with prominence of human inequality lower (i.e. better) than in these.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, <a href="/wiki/List_of_freedom_indices" title="List of freedom indices">Human Freedom Index</a> published by the <a href="/wiki/Cato_Institute" title="Cato Institute">Cato Institute</a> Armenia ranked 29th for economic freedom and 76th for personal freedom among 159 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Armenia ranks 47th on <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">Doing Business</a> Index in 2018 with 13th rank on "starting business" sub-index.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> (CPI), Armenia ranked 95 of 168 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>, Armenia ranked 54th, ahead of countries like France, Portugal and Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-economic-index_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economic-index-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Science.2C_technology_and_education"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Science,_technology_and_education">Science, technology and education</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Armenia" title="Science and technology in Armenia">Science and technology in Armenia</a></div>\n<p>Research spending is low in Armenia, averaging 0.25% of GDP over 2010\xe2\x80\x932013. However, the statistical record of research expenditure is incomplete, as expenditure by privately owned business enterprises is not surveyed in Armenia. The world average for domestic expenditure on research was 1.7% of GDP in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:GERD%20GDP%20ratio%20for%20the%20Black%20Sea%20countries,%202001%E2%80%932013.svg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg/220px-GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg.png" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg/330px-GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg/440px-GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="486" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries,_2001%E2%80%932013.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GERD GDP ratio for the Black Sea countries, 2001\xe2\x80\x932013. Source: UNESCO Science Report: towards 2030 (2015), Figure 12.3</div></div></div>\n<p>The country\'s <i>Strategy for the Development of Science 2011\xe2\x80\x932020</i> envisions that \xe2\x80\x98by 2020, Armenia is a country with a knowledge-based economy and is competitive within the European Research Area with its level of basic and applied research.\xe2\x80\x99 It fixes the following targets:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Creation of a system capable of sustaining the development of science and technology;</li>\n<li>Development of scientific potential, modernization of scientific infrastructure;</li>\n<li>Promotion of basic and applied research;</li>\n<li>Creation of a synergistic system of education, science and innovation; and</li>\n<li>Becoming a prime location for scientific specialization in the European Research Area.</li></ul>\n<p>Based on this strategy, the accompanying <i>Action Plan</i> was approved by the government in June 2011. It defines the following targets:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Improve the management system for science and technology and create the requisite conditions for sustainable development;</li>\n<li>Involve more young, talented people in education and research, while upgrading research infrastructure;</li>\n<li>Create the requisite conditions for the development of an integrated national innovation system; and</li>\n<li>Enhance international co-operation in research and development.</li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:GERD%20in%20the%20Black%20Sea%20region%20by%20sector%20of%20performance,%202005%20and%202013.svg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg/220px-GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg.png" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg/330px-GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg/440px-GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="633" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance,_2005_and_2013.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GERD in the Black Sea region by sector of performance, 2005 and 2013. Source: UNESCO Science Report: towards 2030 (2015), Figure 12.5</div></div></div>\n<p>Although the <i>Strategy</i> clearly pursues a \xe2\x80\x98science push\xe2\x80\x99 approach, with public research institutes serving as the key policy target, it nevertheless mentions the goal of establishing an innovation system. However, the main driver of innovation, the business sector, is not mentioned. In between publishing the <i>Strategy</i> and <i>Action Plan</i>, the government issued a resolution in May 2010 on <i>Science and Technology Development Priorities for 2010\xe2\x80\x932014</i>. These priorities are:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_133-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Armenian studies, humanities and social sciences;</li>\n<li>Life sciences;</li>\n<li>Renewable energy, new energy sources;</li>\n<li>Advanced technologies, information technologies;</li>\n<li>Space, Earth sciences, sustainable use of natural resources; and</li>\n<li>Basic research promoting essential applied research.</li></ul>\n<p>The Law on the National Academy of Sciences was adopted in May 2011. This law is expected to play a key role in shaping the Armenian innovation system. It allows the National Academy of Sciences to extend its business activities to the commercialization of research results and the creation of spin-offs; it also makes provision for restructuring the National Academy of Sciences by combining institutes involved in closely related research areas into a single body. Three of these new centres are particularly relevant: the Centre for Biotechnology, the Centre for Zoology and Hydro-ecology and the Centre for Organic and Pharmaceutical Chemistry.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_133-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government is focusing its support on selected industrial sectors. More than 20 projects have been cofunded by the State Committee of Science in targeted branches: pharmaceuticals, medicine and biotechnology, agricultural mechanization and machine building, electronics, engineering, chemistry and, in particular, the sphere of information technology.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_133-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Over the past decade, the government has made an effort to encourage science\xe2\x80\x93industry linkages. The Armenian information technology sector has been particularly active: a number of public\xe2\x80\x93private partnerships have been established between companies and universities, in order to give students marketable skills and generate innovative ideas at the interface of science and business. Examples are Synopsys Inc. and the Enterprise Incubator Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_133-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%A2_%D5%A1%D6%82%D5%A1%D5%A3_%D5%A4%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%B8%D6%81.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%A2_%D5%A1%D6%82%D5%A1%D5%A3_%D5%A4%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%B8%D6%81.jpg/220px-%D4%B1%D5%B5%D5%A2_%D5%A1%D6%82%D5%A1%D5%A3_%D5%A4%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%B8%D6%81.jpg"
