School</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UWC_Dilijan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/UWC_Dilijan.jpg/220px-UWC_Dilijan.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/UWC_Dilijan.jpg/330px-UWC_Dilijan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/UWC_Dilijan.jpg/440px-UWC_Dilijan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UWC_Dilijan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/UWC_Dilijan" title="UWC Dilijan">UWC Dilijan</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg/220px-Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg/330px-Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg/440px-Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4814" data-file-height="2708" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies" title="Tumo Center for Creative Technologies">Tumo Center for Creative Technologies</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:American_University_of_Armenia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/American_University_of_Armenia.JPG/220px-American_University_of_Armenia.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/American_University_of_Armenia.JPG/330px-American_University_of_Armenia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/American_University_of_Armenia.JPG/440px-American_University_of_Armenia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3392" data-file-height="2264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:American_University_of_Armenia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Armenia" title="American University of Armenia">American University of Armenia</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Armenia" title="Education in Armenia">Education in Armenia</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span></h4>\n<p>In medieval times <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gladzor" title="University of Gladzor">University of Gladzor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tatev_Monastery#Tatev_University" title="Tatev Monastery">University of Tatev</a> took an important role for whole Armenia.\n</p><p>A literacy rate of 100% was reported as early as 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">In the communist era</a>, Armenian education followed the standard Soviet model of complete state control (from Moscow) of <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curricula</a> and teaching methods and close integration of education activities with other aspects of society, such as politics, culture, and the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1988\xe2\x80\x9389 school year, 301 students per 10,000 population were in specialized secondary or higher education, a figure slightly lower than the Soviet average.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In 1989 some 58% of Armenians over age fifteen had completed their secondary education, and 14% had a higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In the 1990\xe2\x80\x9391 school year, the estimated 1,307 primary and secondary schools were attended by 608,800 students.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Another seventy specialised secondary institutions had 45,900 students, and 68,400 students were enrolled in a total of ten postsecondary institutions that included universities.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In addition, 35% of eligible children attended <a href="/wiki/Preschool_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Preschool education">preschools</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In 1992 Armenia\'s largest institution of higher learning, <a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_University" title="Yerevan State University">Yerevan State University</a>, had eighteen departments, including ones for social sciences, sciences, and law.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Its faculty numbered about 1,300 teachers and its student population about 10,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_University_of_Armenia" title="National Polytechnic University of Armenia">National Polytechnic University of Armenia</a> is operating since 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early 1990s, Armenia made substantial changes to the centralised and regimented Soviet system.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Because at least 98% of students in higher education were Armenian, curricula began to emphasise <a href="/wiki/History_of_Armenia" title="History of Armenia">Armenian history</a> and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> became the dominant language of instruction, and many schools that had taught in Russian closed by the end of 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Russian was still widely taught, however, as a second language.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, the National Program for Educational Excellence embarked on creating an internationally competitive and academically rigorous alternative educational program (the Araratian Baccalaureate) for Armenian schools and increase the importance and status of the teacher\'s role in society.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation">Regulation</span></h4>\n<p>The Ministry of Education and Science is responsible for regulation of the sector.\n</p><p>Primary and secondary education in Armenia is free, and completion of secondary school is compulsory.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_134-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>High education in Armenia is harmonized with <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna process</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Armenian_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Armenian National Academy of Sciences">Armenian National Academy of Sciences</a> plays important role in postgraduate education.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_education">Secondary education</span></h4>\n<p>Schooling takes 12 years in Armenia and breaks down into primary (4 years), middle (5 years) and high school (3 years). Schools engage a 10-grade mark system.\n</p><p>Interesting feature of primary and secondary education is obligatory <a href="/wiki/Chess_in_Armenia#Teaching_of_chess_in_schools" title="Chess in Armenia">schooling in chess playing</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/UWC_Dilijan" title="UWC Dilijan">UWC Dilijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayb_School" title="Ayb School">Ayb School</a> and <a href="/wiki/QSI_International_School_of_Yerevan" title="QSI International School of Yerevan">QSI International School of Yerevan</a> are private primary and secondary schools. \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies" title="Tumo Center for Creative Technologies">Tumo Center for Creative Technologies</a> is one of the most prominent auxiliary education concepts in Armenia.\n</p><p>Armath<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> laboratories are a prominent concept for engaging pupils into studying technical sciences and applied technologies.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Teach_For_Armenia" title="Teach For Armenia">Teach for Armenia</a> is works towards the improvement of primary and secondary education enrollment in regions of Armenia.\n</p><p>The Government also supports <a href="/wiki/List_of_Armenian_schools#Schools_outside_Armenia" title="List of Armenian schools">Armenian schools outside of Armenia</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_education">Tertiary education</span></h4>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_universities">Major universities</span></h5>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_University" title="Yerevan State University">Yerevan State University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_Medical_University" title="Yerevan State Medical University">Yerevan State Medical University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Armenian_State_University_of_Economics" title="Armenian State University of Economics">Armenian State University of Economics</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_University_of_Armenia" title="National Polytechnic University of Armenia">National Polytechnic University of Armenia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Architecture_and_Construction_of_Armenia" title="National University of Architecture and Construction of Armenia">National University of Architecture and Construction of Armenia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yerevan_Brusov_State_University_of_Languages_and_Social_Sciences" title="Yerevan Brusov State University of Languages and Social Sciences">Yerevan Brusov State University of Languages and Social Sciences</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Armenian_National_Agrarian_University" title="Armenian National Agrarian University">Armenian National Agrarian University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Armenian_State_Pedagogical_University" title="Armenian State Pedagogical University">Armenian State Pedagogical University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Armenia" title="American University of Armenia">American University of Armenia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Russian-Armenian_(Slavonic)_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian-Armenian (Slavonic) University">Russian-Armenian (Slavonic) University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fondation_Universit%C3%A9_Fran%C3%A7aise_en_Arm%C3%A9nie" title="Fondation Universit\xc3\xa9 Fran\xc3\xa7aise en Arm\xc3\xa9nie">Fondation Universit\xc3\xa9 Fran\xc3\xa7aise en Arm\xc3\xa9nie</a></li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Armenia" title="List of universities in Armenia">List of universities in Armenia</a> includes many other.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="American_University_of_Armenia">American University of Armenia</span></h5>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Armenia" title="American University of Armenia">American University of Armenia</a> has <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate programs</a> in Business and Law, among others. The institution owes its existence to the combined efforts of the Government of Armenia, the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_General_Benevolent_Union" title="Armenian General Benevolent Union">Armenian General Benevolent Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">US Agency for International Development</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a>. The extension programs and the library at AUA form a new focal point for English-language intellectual life in the city. Armenia also hosts a deployment of <a href="/wiki/One_Laptop_per_Child" title="One Laptop per Child">One Laptop per Child</a> initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Yerevan_State_Medical_University">Yerevan State Medical University</span></h5>\n<p>On the basis of the expansion and development of <a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_University" title="Yerevan State University">Yerevan State University</a> a number of higher educational independent Institutions were formed including Medical Institute separated in 1930 which was set up on the basis of medical faculty. In 1980 <a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_Medical_University" title="Yerevan State Medical University">Yerevan State Medical University</a> was awarded one of the main rewards of the former USSR \xe2\x80\x93 the Order of Labor red Banner for training qualified specialists in health care and valuable service in the development of Medical Science. In 1995 YSMI was renamed to YSMU and since 1989 it has been named after <a href="/wiki/Mkhitar_Heratsi" title="Mkhitar Heratsi">Mkhitar Heratsi</a>, the famous medieval doctor. <a href="/wiki/Mkhitar_Heratsi" title="Mkhitar Heratsi">Mkhitar Heratsi</a> was the founder of Armenian Medical school in Cilician Armenia. The great doctor played the same role in Armenian Medical Science as <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> in Western, <a href="/wiki/Galen" title="Galen">Galen</a> in Roman, <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Ibn S\xc4\xabn\xc4\x81</a> in Arabic medicine.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG/220px-ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG/330px-ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG/440px-ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ATC_MAB_Graduates.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graduates of the MAB program of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_National_Agrarian_University" title="Armenian National Agrarian University">Agribusiness Teaching Center</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Foreign students\' department for Armenian diaspora established in 1957 later was enlarged and the enrollment of foreign students began. Nowadays the <a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_Medical_University" title="Yerevan State Medical University">YSMU</a> is a Medical Institution corresponding to international requirements, trains medical staff for not only Armenia and neighbour countries, i.e. Iran, Syria, Lebanon, Georgia, but also many other leading countries all over the world. A great number of foreign students from India, Nepal, Sri Lanka, the USA and Russia study together with Armenian students. Nowadays the university is ranked among famous higher Medical Institutions and takes its honourable place in the World Directory of Medical Schools published by the WHO.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span></h5>\n<p>Gross enrollment in <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary education</a> at 44% in 2015 surpassed peer countries of South Caucasus but remained below of the average for Europe and Central Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>However public spendings per student in tertiary education in GDP-ratio terms is one of the lowest for post-USSR countries (for which data was available).<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Armenia" title="Demographics of Armenia">Demographics of Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>Armenia has a population of 2,924,816 (2016 est.)<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and is the third most densely populated of the former Soviet republics.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> There has been a problem of <a href="/wiki/Population_decline" title="Population decline">population decline</a> due to elevated levels of <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">emigration</a> after the break-up of the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In the past years emigration levels have declined and some population growth is observed since 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ArmenianDiaspora.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/ArmenianDiaspora.png/220px-ArmenianDiaspora.png" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/ArmenianDiaspora.png/330px-ArmenianDiaspora.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/ArmenianDiaspora.png/440px-ArmenianDiaspora.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ArmenianDiaspora.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian population around the world</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Armenia has <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">a relatively large external diaspora</a> (8&#160;million by some estimates, greatly exceeding the 3&#160;million population of Armenia itself), with communities existing across the globe. The largest Armenian communities outside of Armenia can be found in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>,\n<a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>. 40,000 to 70,000 Armenians still live in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (mostly in and around <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>About 1,000 Armenians reside in the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Quarter" title="Armenian Quarter">Armenian Quarter</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Jerusalem)" title="Old City (Jerusalem)">Old City</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, a remnant of a once-larger community.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Italy is home to the <a href="/wiki/San_Lazzaro_degli_Armeni" title="San Lazzaro degli Armeni">San Lazzaro degli Armeni</a>, an island located in the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Lagoon" title="Venetian Lagoon">Venetian Lagoon</a>, which is completely occupied by a monastery run by the <a href="/wiki/Mechitarists" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechitarists">Mechitarists</a>, an Armenian Catholic congregation.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Approximately 139,000 Armenians live in the de facto independent country <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Republic of Artsakh</a> where they form a majority.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_distribution_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Armenian_distribution_map.png/220px-Armenian_distribution_map.png" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Armenian_distribution_map.png/330px-Armenian_distribution_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Armenian_distribution_map.png/440px-Armenian_distribution_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="921" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_distribution_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>Historical and modern distribution of Armenians.<br /></b>Settlement area of Armenians in early 20th century:<br /><span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #967117; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;&gt;50%<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span><span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFA700; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;25\xe2\x80\x9350%<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span><span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FBEC5D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;&lt;25%<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Armenian settlement area today.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Ethnic <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> make up 98.1% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Yazidi" class="mw-redirect" title="Yazidi">Yazidis</a> make up 1.2%, and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> 0.4%. Other minorities include <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontic_Greeks" title="Pontic Greeks">Greeks</a> (usually called <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Greeks" title="Caucasus Greeks">Caucasus Greeks</a>), <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Armenia" title="History of the Jews in Armenia">Jews</a>. There are also smaller communities of <a href="/wiki/Vlachs" title="Vlachs">Vlachs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mordvins" title="Mordvins">Mordvins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udi_people" title="Udi people">Udis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tat_people_(Caucasus)" title="Tat people (Caucasus)">Tats</a>. Minorities of <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Germans" title="Caucasus Germans">Caucasus Germans</a> also exist though they are heavily <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russified</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-minorities_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minorities-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there are an estimated 35,000 Yazidis in Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet era">Soviet era</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a> were historically the second largest population in the country (forming about 2.5% in 1989).<sup id="cite_ref-1989census_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1989census-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> However, due to the conflict over <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>, virtually all of them emigrated from Armenia to Azerbaijan. Conversely, Armenia received a large influx of Armenian refugees from Azerbaijan, thus giving Armenia a more homogeneous character.\n</p><p>According to Gallup research conducted in 2017 Armenia has one of the highest migrant acceptance (welcoming) rates in eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Armenia" title="Languages of Armenia">Languages of Armenia</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> is the only official language. The main foreign languages that Armenians know are Russian and English. Due to its Soviet past, most of the old population can speak Russian quite well. According to a 2013 survey, 95% of Armenians said they had some knowledge of Russian (24% advanced, 59% intermediate) compared to 40% who said they knew some English (4% advanced, 16% intermediate and 20% beginner). However, more adults (50%) think that English should be taught in public secondary schools than those who prefer Russian (44%).<sup id="cite_ref-2012_knowledge_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012_knowledge-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Armenia" title="Religion in Armenia">Religion in Armenia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kohrvirab.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kohrvirab.jpg/220px-Kohrvirab.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kohrvirab.jpg/330px-Kohrvirab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kohrvirab.jpg/440px-Kohrvirab.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kohrvirab.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 7th-century <a href="/wiki/Khor_Virap" title="Khor Virap">Khor Virap</a> monastery in the shadow of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a>, the peak on which <a href="/wiki/Noah%27s_Ark" title="Noah&#39;s Ark">Noah\'s Ark</a> is said to have landed during the <a href="/wiki/Genesis_flood_narrative" title="Genesis flood narrative">biblical flood</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Armenia was the first nation to adopt Christianity as a state religion, an event traditionally dated to AD 301.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The predominant <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Armenia" title="Religion in Armenia">religion in Armenia</a> is Christianity. The roots of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Church</a> go back to the 1st century. According to tradition, the Armenian Church was founded by two of Jesus\' twelve <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Apostles" class="mw-redirect" title="Twelve Apostles">apostles</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Jude_the_Apostle" title="Jude the Apostle">Thaddaeus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_the_Apostle" title="Bartholomew the Apostle">Bartholomew</a> \xe2\x80\x93 who preached Christianity in Armenia between AD 40\xe2\x80\x9360. Because of these two founding apostles, the official name of the Armenian Church is <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>.\n</p><p>Over 93% of Armenian Christians belong to the Armenian Apostolic Church, a form of Oriental (Non-<a href="/wiki/Chalcedonian_Christianity" title="Chalcedonian Christianity">Chalcedonian</a>) Orthodoxy, which is a very ritualistic, conservative church, roughly comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">Coptic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Orthodox_Church" title="Syriac Orthodox Church">Syriac</a> churches.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The Armenian Apostolic Church is in communion only with a group of churches within <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy#Oriental_Orthodox_Communion" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodoxy</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Evangelical_Church" title="Armenian Evangelical Church">Armenian Evangelical Church</a> has a very sizeable and favourable presence among the life of Armenians with over several thousand members throughout the country. It traces its roots back to 1846 which was under patronage of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Armenian Patriarchate of Constantinople">Armenian Patriarchate of Constantinople</a> the aim of which was to train qualified clergy for the Armenian Apostolic Church.\n</p><p>Other Christian denominations practising faith based on Nicene Creed in Armenia are the Pentecostal branches of Protestant community such as the Word of Life, the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Brotherhood_Church" title="Armenian Brotherhood Church">Armenian Brotherhood Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> which are known as of the oldest existing denominations in Armenia and were permitted by the authorities of Soviet Union,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Presbyterians" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterians">Presbyterians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Catholics also exist in Armenia, both <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin rite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_rite" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian rite">Armenian rite</a> Catholics. The <a href="/wiki/Mechitarists" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechitarists">Mechitarists</a> (also spelled "Mekhitarists" <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">\xd5\x84\xd5\xad\xd5\xab\xd5\xa9\xd5\xa1\xd6\x80\xd5\xa5\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb6</span>), are a congregation of <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Benedict" title="Order of Saint Benedict">Benedictine</a> monks of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Catholic_Church" title="Armenian Catholic Church">Armenian Catholic Church</a> founded in 1712 by <a href="/wiki/Mekhitar_of_Sebaste" class="mw-redirect" title="Mekhitar of Sebaste">Mekhitar of Sebaste</a>. They are best known for their series of scholarly publications of ancient <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenian</a> versions of otherwise lost ancient Greek texts.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Catholic_Church" title="Armenian Catholic Church">Armenian Catholic</a> denomination is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Bzoummar" title="Bzoummar">Bzoummar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>.\n</p><p>Armenia is home to a <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Armenia" title="Russians in Armenia">Russian</a> community of <a href="/wiki/Molokan" title="Molokan">Molokans</a> which practice a form of Spiritual Christianity originated from the Russian Orthodox Church.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Yazidis, who live in the western part of the country, practice <a href="/wiki/Yazidism" class="mw-redirect" title="Yazidism">Yazidism</a>. As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the world\'s largest Yazidi temple is under construction in the small village of Aknalish.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> There are also Kurds who practice <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>There is a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Armenia" title="History of the Jews in Armenia">Jewish community in Armenia</a> diminished to 750 persons since independence with most emigrants leaving for Israel. There are currently two synagogues in Armenia \xe2\x80\x93 in the capital, Yerevan, and in the city of <a href="/wiki/Sevan_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sevan (city)">Sevan</a> located near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Sevan" title="Lake Sevan">Lake Sevan</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>\n<p>Vast improvements of health services occurred in the past decade. Such improvements consisted of easier accessibility to health-care services and an Open Enrollment program which allows Armenians to freely choose their healthcare service provider.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Certified by <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> Armenia was the first<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> in European region and as of October 2017 is one of 10 countries worldwide (7 of which are islands) which proved to have eliminated <a href="/wiki/Vertically_transmitted_infection" title="Vertically transmitted infection">mother-to-child</a> <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> transmission.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to WHO data <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality rate</a> nearly halved from 2002 to 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Health expenditures at 4.5% of GDP in 2014 were 3rd lowest in post-USSR countries and below the average of the region of Europe and Central Asia, same as in years 2006\xe2\x80\x932013.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Health expenditures as percentage of government spendings were 4th lowest for the same group in 2008\xe2\x80\x932014, but beat peers in <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">South Caucasus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Health expenditures in per capita terms (at PPP at constant 2005 USD) were nearly permanently 5th lowest in the above group in years 1999\xe2\x80\x932014.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Out-of-pocket health expenditure were 4th highest in the same group in years 2003\xe2\x80\x932006 and 2010\xe2\x80\x932014.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> In 2014 4.3% of health expenditures came from sources outside of Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">Undernourishment</a> at 6.3% in 2014 of population remained nearly unchanged since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">Obesity</a> rate is 19.5% in Armenia in 2017, which is lower than in all regional countries and nearly all European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Policy_in_Armenia" title="Tobacco Policy in Armenia">Tobacco policy in Armenia</a> is as of February 2018 still very permissive with almost no enforcement of any smoke-restricting laws.\n</p><p>After significant decline crude in earlier decades crude birth rates remained at 13.0\xe2\x80\x9314.2 per 1000 people nearly constant in years 1998\xe2\x80\x932015.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> In the same period crude death rate went from 8.6 to 9.3 per 1000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Note that crude rates are not age-adjusted.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy at birth</a> at 74.8 years was 4th highest among post-USSR countries in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Armenia" title="Culture of Armenia">Culture of Armenia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET,_OSHAKAN,_ARMENIA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET%2C_OSHAKAN%2C_ARMENIA.jpg/220px-THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET%2C_OSHAKAN%2C_ARMENIA.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET%2C_OSHAKAN%2C_ARMENIA.jpg/330px-THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET%2C_OSHAKAN%2C_ARMENIA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET%2C_OSHAKAN%2C_ARMENIA.jpg/440px-THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET%2C_OSHAKAN%2C_ARMENIA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:THE_ARMENIAN_ALPHABET,_OSHAKAN,_ARMENIA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Armenian_alphabet" title="Armenian alphabet">Armenian alphabet</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Armenians have their own distinctive <a href="/wiki/Armenian_alphabet" title="Armenian alphabet">alphabet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">language</a>. The alphabet was invented in AD 405 by <a href="/wiki/Mesrop_Mashtots" title="Mesrop Mashtots">Mesrop Mashtots</a> and consists of thirty-nine letters, three of which were added during the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cilicia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Cilicia">Cilician period</a>. 96% of the people in the country speak Armenian, while 75.8% of the population additionally speaks Russian, although English is becoming increasingly popular.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Armenia" title="Media of Armenia">Media of Armenia</a></div>\n<p>Television, magazines, and newspapers are all operated by both state-owned and for-profit corporations which depend on <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subscription" class="mw-redirect" title="Subscription">subscription</a>, and other sales-related revenues. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Armenia" title="Constitution of Armenia">Constitution of Armenia</a> guarantees freedom of speech and Armenia ranks 78th in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> report compiled by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\nAs a <a href="/wiki/Transition_economy" title="Transition economy">country in transition</a>, Armenia\'s media system is under transformation.<sup id="cite_ref-EJC_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EJC-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Frequent attacks on journalists of non-state sponsored media is a serious threat to Armenia\'s press freedom. The number of assaults has recently declined, but the physical integrity of journalists remain at stake.<sup id="cite_ref-pace_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pace-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Armenia" title="Music of Armenia">Music of Armenia</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:567px;max-width:567px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:200px;max-width:200px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Djivan_Gasparyan_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Djivan_Gasparyan_2009.jpg/396px-Djivan_Gasparyan_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Sirusho_Harutyunyan_at_Eurovision_2008_8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Sirusho_Harutyunyan_at_Eurovision_2008_8.jpg/180px-Sirusho_Harutyunyan_at_Eurovision_2008_8.jpg" width="180" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Sirusho_Harutyunyan_at_Eurovision_2008_8.jpg/270px-Sirusho_Harutyunyan_at_Eurovision_2008_8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Sirusho_Harutyunyan_at_Eurovision_2008_8.jpg/360px-Sirusho_Harutyunyan_at_Eurovision_2008_8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2880" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:179px;max-width:179px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:2014.06.23._Charles_Aznavour_Fot_Mariusz_Kubik_09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/2014.06.23._Charles_Aznavour_Fot_Mariusz_Kubik_09.jpg/177px-2014.06.23._Charles_Aznavour_Fot_Mariusz_Kubik_09.jpg" width="177" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/2014.06.23._Charles_Aznavour_Fot_Mariusz_Kubik_09.jpg/266px-2014.06.23._Charles_Aznavour_Fot_Mariusz_Kubik_09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/2014.06.23._Charles_Aznavour_Fot_Mariusz_Kubik_09.jpg/354px-2014.06.23._Charles_Aznavour_Fot_Mariusz_Kubik_09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Djivan_Gasparyan" title="Djivan Gasparyan">Djivan Gasparyan</a> (left), <a href="/wiki/Sirusho" title="Sirusho">Sirusho</a> (middle) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Aznavour" title="Charles Aznavour">Charles Aznavour</a> (right) are among most popular musicians of Armenia.</div></div></div>\n<p>Armenian music is a mix of indigenous folk music, perhaps best-represented by <a href="/wiki/Djivan_Gasparyan" title="Djivan Gasparyan">Djivan Gasparyan</a>\'s well-known <a href="/wiki/Duduk" title="Duduk">duduk</a> music, as well as light pop, and extensive <a href="/wiki/Christian_music" title="Christian music">Christian music</a>.\n</p><p>Instruments like the duduk, <a href="/wiki/Dhol" title="Dhol">dhol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zurna" title="Zurna">zurna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kanun_(instrument)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanun (instrument)">kanun</a> are commonly found in Armenian folk music. Artists such as <a href="/wiki/Sayat_Nova" class="mw-redirect" title="Sayat Nova">Sayat Nova</a> are famous due to their influence in the development of Armenian folk music. One of the oldest types of Armenian music is the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_chant" title="Armenian chant">Armenian chant</a> which is the most common kind of religious music in Armenia. Many of these chants are ancient in origin, extending to pre-Christian times, while others are relatively modern, including several composed by Saint Mesrop Mashtots, the inventor of the Armenian alphabet. Whilst under <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> rule, the Armenian classical music composer <a href="/wiki/Aram_Khatchaturian" class="mw-redirect" title="Aram Khatchaturian">Aram Khatchaturian</a> became internationally well known for his music, for various ballets and the <a href="/wiki/Sabre_Dance" title="Sabre Dance">Sabre Dance</a> from his composition for the ballet <a href="/wiki/Gayane_(ballet)" title="Gayane (ballet)">Gayane</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg/220px-Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg/330px-Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg/440px-Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armeniapedia_dance2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Armenian_dance" title="Armenian dance">Armenian dance</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Armenian Genocide caused widespread emigration that led to the settlement of Armenians in various countries in the world. Armenians kept to their traditions and certain diasporans rose to fame with their music. In the post-Genocide Armenian community of the United States, the so-called "kef" style Armenian dance music, using Armenian and Middle Eastern folk instruments (often electrified/amplified) and some western instruments, was popular. This style preserved the folk songs and dances of <a href="/wiki/Western_Armenia" title="Western Armenia">Western Armenia</a>, and many artists also played the contemporary popular songs of Turkey and other Middle Eastern countries from which the Armenians emigrated.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Richard_Hagopian" title="Richard Hagopian">Richard Hagopian</a> is perhaps the most famous artist of the traditional "kef" style and the Vosbikian Band was notable in the 1940s and 1950s for developing their own style of "kef music" heavily influenced by the popular American <a href="/wiki/Big_Band" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Band">Big Band</a> Jazz of the time. Later, stemming from the Middle Eastern Armenian diaspora and influenced by Continental European (especially French) pop music, the Armenian pop music genre grew to fame in the 1960s and 1970s with artists such as <a href="/wiki/Adiss_Harmandian" title="Adiss Harmandian">Adiss Harmandian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harout_Pamboukjian" title="Harout Pamboukjian">Harout Pamboukjian</a> performing to the Armenian diaspora and Armenia; also with artists such as <a href="/wiki/Sirusho" title="Sirusho">Sirusho</a>, performing pop music combined with Armenian folk music in today\'s entertainment industry.\n</p><p>Other Armenian diasporans that rose to fame in classical or international music circles are world-renowned <a href="/wiki/List_of_French-Armenians" class="mw-redirect" title="List of French-Armenians">French-Armenian</a> singer and composer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Aznavour" title="Charles Aznavour">Charles Aznavour</a>, pianist <a href="/wiki/Sahan_Arzruni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahan Arzruni">Sahan Arzruni</a>, prominent opera sopranos such as <a href="/wiki/Hasmik_Papian" title="Hasmik Papian">Hasmik Papian</a> and more recently <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Bayrakdarian" title="Isabel Bayrakdarian">Isabel Bayrakdarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anna_Kasyan" title="Anna Kasyan">Anna Kasyan</a>. Certain Armenians settled to sing non-Armenian tunes such as the heavy metal band <a href="/wiki/System_of_a_Down" title="System of a Down">System of a Down</a> (which nonetheless often incorporates traditional Armenian instrumentals and styling into their songs) or pop star <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>. In the Armenian diaspora, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Revolutionary Songs">Armenian revolutionary songs</a> are popular with the youth. These songs encourage Armenian patriotism and are generally about Armenian history and national heroes.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_art" title="Armenian art">Armenian art</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Armenia" title="List of museums in Armenia">List of museums in Armenia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG/170px-Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG/255px-Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG/340px-Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Khachkar-raffi_kojian-IMG_0513.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient Armenian <a href="/wiki/Khachkar" title="Khachkar">Khachkars</a> (cross-stones)</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Yerevan_Vernissage" title="Yerevan Vernissage">Yerevan Vernissage</a> (arts and crafts market), close to Republic Square, bustles with hundreds of vendors selling a variety of crafts on weekends and Wednesdays (though the selection is much reduced mid-week). The market offers woodcarving, antiques, fine lace, and the hand-knotted wool carpets and kilims that are a Caucasus speciality. <a href="/wiki/Obsidian" title="Obsidian">Obsidian</a>, which is found locally, is crafted into assortment of jewellery and ornamental objects. Armenian gold smithery enjoys a long tradition, populating one corner of the market with a selection of gold items. Soviet relics and souvenirs of recent Russian manufacture \xe2\x80\x93 nesting dolls, watches, enamel boxes and so on \xe2\x80\x93 are also available at the Vernisage.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zabel_return.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Zabel_return.jpg/220px-Zabel_return.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Zabel_return.jpg/330px-Zabel_return.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Zabel_return.jpg/440px-Zabel_return.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1075" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zabel_return.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Isabella,_Queen_of_Armenia" title="Isabella, Queen of Armenia">Queen Zabel</a>\xe2\x80\x99s Return to the Palace</i>, <a href="/wiki/Vardges_Sureniants" title="Vardges Sureniants">Vardges Sureniants</a>, (1909)</div></div></div>\n<p>Across from the Opera House, a popular art market fills another city park on the weekends. Armenia\xe2\x80\x99s long history as a crossroads of the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">ancient world</a> has resulted in a landscape with innumerable fascinating <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_site" title="Archaeological site">archaeological sites</a> to explore. <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Medieval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> and even <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> sites are all within a few hours drive from the city. All but the most spectacular remain virtually undiscovered, allowing visitors to view churches and fortresses in their original settings.\n</p><p>The National Art Gallery in Yerevan has more than 16,000 works that date back to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, which indicate Armenia\'s rich tales and stories of the times. It houses paintings by many <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a> masters as well. The Modern Art Museum, the Children\xe2\x80\x99s Picture Gallery, and the <a href="/wiki/Martiros_Saryan" title="Martiros Saryan">Martiros Saryan</a> Museum are only a few of the other noteworthy collections of fine art on display in Yerevan. Moreover, many private galleries are in operation, with many more opening every year, featuring rotating exhibitions and sales.\n</p><p>On 13 April 2013, the Armenian government announced a change in law to allow <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_panorama" title="Freedom of panorama">freedom of panorama</a> for 3D works of art.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Armenia" title="Cinema of Armenia">Cinema of Armenia</a></div>\n<p>Cinema in Armenia was born on April 16, 1923, when the Armenian State Committee of Cinema was established by a decree of the Soviet Armenian government.\n</p><p>However, the first Armenian film with Armenian subject called "Haykakan Sinema" was produced earlier in 1912 in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> by Armenian-Egyptian publisher Vahan Zartarian. The film was premiered in Cairo on March 13, 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 1924, the first Armenian film studio; <i><a href="/wiki/Armenfilm" title="Armenfilm">Armenfilm</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">\xd5\x80\xd5\xa1\xd5\xb5\xd6\x86\xd5\xab\xd5\xac\xd5\xb4</span> "Hayfilm," <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">\xd0\x90\xd1\x80\xd0\xbc\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbd\xd0\xba\xd0\xb8\xd0\xbd\xd0\xbe</span> "Armenkino") was established in Yerevan, starting with a <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentary film</a> called <i>Soviet Armenia</i>.\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Namus_(film)" title="Namus (film)">Namus</a></i> was the first Armenian <a href="/wiki/Silent_film" title="Silent film">silent</a> <a href="/wiki/Black-and-white" class="mw-redirect" title="Black-and-white">black-and-white</a> film, directed by <a href="/wiki/Hamo_Beknazarian" title="Hamo Beknazarian">Hamo Beknazarian</a> in 1925, based on a play of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Shirvanzade" title="Alexander Shirvanzade">Alexander Shirvanzade</a>, describing the ill fate of two lovers, who were engaged by their families to each other since childhood, but because of violations of <i><a href="/wiki/Namus" title="Namus">namus</a></i> (a tradition of honor), the girl was married by her father to another person. The first <a href="/wiki/Sound_film" title="Sound film">sound film</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pepo_(film)" title="Pepo (film)">Pepo</a></i> was shot in 1935, director <a href="/wiki/Hamo_Beknazarian" title="Hamo Beknazarian">Hamo Beknazarian</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Armenia" title="Sport in Armenia">Sport in Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chess_in_Armenia" title="Chess in Armenia">Chess in Armenia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg/220px-Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg/330px-Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg/440px-Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2296" data-file-height="1138" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tsaghkadzor_Olympic_Sports_complex.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Tsaghkadzor Olympic Sports complex</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg/220px-Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg/330px-Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg/440px-Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ireland_Armenia_teams.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Armenia_national_football_team" title="Armenia national football team">Armenia national football team</a> in Dublin, Ireland</div></div></div>\n<p>A wide array of sports are played in Armenia, the most popular among them being wrestling, weightlifting, judo, association football, chess, and boxing. Armenia\'s mountainous terrain provides great opportunities for the practice of sports like skiing and climbing. Being a landlocked country, water sports can only be practised on lakes, notably <a href="/wiki/Lake_Sevan" title="Lake Sevan">Lake Sevan</a>. Competitively, Armenia has been successful in chess, weightlifting and wrestling at the international level. Armenia is also an active member of the international sports community, with full membership in the Union of European Football Associations (<a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>) and International Ice Hockey Federation (<a href="/wiki/IIHF" class="mw-redirect" title="IIHF">IIHF</a>). It also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Pan-Armenian_Games" title="Pan-Armenian Games">Pan-Armenian Games</a>.\n</p><p>Prior to 1992, Armenians would participate in the Olympics representing the USSR. As part of the Soviet Union, Armenia was very successful, winning plenty of medals and helping the USSR win the medal standings at the Olympics on numerous occasions. The first medal won by an Armenian in modern Olympic history was by <a href="/wiki/Hrant_Shahinyan" title="Hrant Shahinyan">Hrant Shahinyan</a> (sometimes spelled as Grant Shaginyan), who won two golds and two silvers in gymnastics at the <a href="/wiki/1952_Summer_Olympics" title="1952 Summer Olympics">1952 Summer Olympics</a> in Helsinki. To highlight the level of success of Armenians in the Olympics, Shahinyan was quoted as saying:\n</p><p>"Armenian sportsmen had to outdo their opponents by several notches for the shot at being accepted into any Soviet team. But those difficulties notwithstanding, 90 percent of Armenian athletes on Soviet Olympic teams came back with medals."<sup id="cite_ref-ArmeniaNow.com_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArmeniaNow.com-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Armenia first participated at the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> in Barcelona under a unified CIS team, where it was very successful, winning three golds and one silver in weightlifting, wrestling and sharp shooting, despite only having five athletes. Since the <a href="/wiki/1994_Winter_Olympics" title="1994 Winter Olympics">1994 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lillehammer" title="Lillehammer">Lillehammer</a>, Armenia has participated as an independent nation.\n</p><p>Armenia participates in the Summer Olympic Games in boxing, wrestling, weightlifting, judo, gymnastics, track and field, diving, swimming and sharp shooting. It also participates in the Winter Olympic Games in alpine skiing, cross-country skiing and figure skating.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg/180px-Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg" width="180" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg/270px-Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg/360px-Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Levon_Aronian_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chess Grandmaster <a href="/wiki/Levon_Aronian" title="Levon Aronian">Levon Aronian</a> is a <a href="/wiki/FIDE" title="FIDE">FIDE</a> #2 rated player and the <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_top_chess_players_throughout_history#Elo_system" title="Comparison of top chess players throughout history">fourth highest rated player in history</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Football_in_Armenia" title="Football in Armenia">Football</a> is also popular in Armenia. The most successful team was the <a href="/wiki/FC_Ararat_Yerevan" title="FC Ararat Yerevan">FC Ararat Yerevan</a> team of the 1970s who won the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Cup" title="Soviet Cup">Soviet Cup</a> in 1973 and 1975 and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League_1973" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Top League 1973">Soviet Top League</a> in 1973. The latter achievement saw FC Ararat gain entry to the <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_1974%E2%80%9375" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup 1974\xe2\x80\x9375">European Cup</a> where \xe2\x80\x93 despite a home victory in the second leg \xe2\x80\x93 they lost on aggregate at the quarter final stage to eventual winner <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">FC Bayern Munich</a>. Armenia competed internationally as part of the <a href="/wiki/USSR_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR national football team">USSR national football team</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian national football team">Armenian national football team</a> was formed in 1992 after the split of the Soviet Union. Armenia have never qualified for a major tournament although recent improvements saw the team to achieve 44th position in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a> in September 2011. The national team is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Armenia" title="Football Federation of Armenia">Football Federation of Armenia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Premier_League" title="Armenian Premier League">Armenian Premier League</a> is the highest level football competition in Armenia, and has been dominated by <a href="/wiki/FC_Pyunik" title="FC Pyunik">FC Pyunik</a> in recent seasons. The league currently consists of eight teams and relegates to the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_First_League" title="Armenian First League">Armenian First League</a>.\n</p><p>Armenia and the Armenian diaspora have produced many successful footballers, including <a href="/wiki/Youri_Djorkaeff" title="Youri Djorkaeff">Youri Djorkaeff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alain_Boghossian" title="Alain Boghossian">Alain Boghossian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andranik_Eskandarian" title="Andranik Eskandarian">Andranik Eskandarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andranik_Teymourian" title="Andranik Teymourian">Andranik Teymourian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Manucharyan" title="Edgar Manucharyan">Edgar Manucharyan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Simonyan" title="Nikita Simonyan">Nikita Simonyan</a>. Djokaeff and Boghossian won the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a> with <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>, Andranik Teymourian competed in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> for <a href="/wiki/Iran_national_football_team" title="Iran national football team">Iran</a> and Edgar Manucharyan played in the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> for <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">Wrestling</a> has been a successful sport in the Olympics for Armenia. At the <a href="/wiki/Armenia_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics" title="Armenia at the 1996 Summer Olympics">1996 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armen_Nazaryan" title="Armen Nazaryan">Armen Nazaryan</a> won the gold in the Men\'s <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_wrestling" title="Greco-Roman wrestling">Greco-Roman</a> Flyweight (52&#160;kg) category and <a href="/wiki/Armen_Mkrtchyan" title="Armen Mkrtchyan">Armen Mkrtchyan</a> won the silver in Men\'s <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_wrestling" title="Freestyle wrestling">Freestyle</a> Paperweight (48&#160;kg) category, securing Armenia\'s first two medals in its Olympic history.\n</p><p>Traditional Armenian wrestling is called Kokh and practised in traditional garb; it was one of the influences included in the Soviet combat sport of <a href="/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art)" title="Sambo (martial art)">Sambo</a>, which is also very popular.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Armenia" title="Politics of Armenia">government of Armenia</a> budgets about $2.8&#160;million annually for sports and gives it to the National Committee of Physical Education and Sports, the body that determines which programs should benefit from the funds.<sup id="cite_ref-ArmeniaNow.com_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArmeniaNow.com-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the lack of success lately on the international level, in recent years, Armenia has rebuilt 16 Soviet-era sports schools and furnished them with new equipment for a total cost of $1.9&#160;million. The rebuilding of the regional schools was financed by the Armenian government. $9.3&#160;million has been invested in the resort town of <a href="/wiki/Tsaghkadzor" title="Tsaghkadzor">Tsaghkadzor</a> to improve the <a href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">winter sports</a> infrastructure because of dismal performances at recent <a href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">winter sports</a> events. In 2005, a cycling centre was opened in <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> with the aim of helping produce world class Armenian cyclists. The government has also promised a cash reward of $700,000 to Armenians who win a gold medal at the Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-ArmeniaNow.com_194-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArmeniaNow.com-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Armenia has also been very successful in chess, winning the <a href="/wiki/World_Team_Chess_Championship" title="World Team Chess Championship">World Champion</a> in 2011 and the <a href="/wiki/Chess_Olympiad" title="Chess Olympiad">World Chess Olympiad</a> on three occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_cuisine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Armenian_cuisine.jpg/220px-Armenian_cuisine.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Armenian_cuisine.jpg/330px-Armenian_cuisine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Armenian_cuisine.jpg/440px-Armenian_cuisine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_cuisine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Armenian cuisine</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_cuisine" title="Armenian cuisine">Armenian cuisine</a></div>\n<p>Armenian cuisine is closely related to eastern and <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_cuisine" title="Mediterranean cuisine">Mediterranean cuisine</a>; various <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruits</a> combine to present unique dishes. The main characteristics of Armenian cuisine are a reliance on the quality of the ingredients rather than heavily spicing food, the use of herbs, the use of wheat in a variety of forms, of legumes, nuts, and fruit (as a main ingredient as well as to sour food), and the stuffing of a wide variety of leaves.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate" title="Pomegranate">pomegranate</a>, with its symbolic association with fertility, represents that nation. The <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">apricot</a> is the national fruit.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div
